YWCA Bergen County Empowers Girls to Live Active, Healthy Lives
February 6, 2013

Tags: american red cross, aquatics, classes, confidence, empowerment, girls, health, instructor, lifeguard, lisa prins, power, sports, swimming, Title IX, women and girls in sports day, ywca bergen 



By Helen Archontou, MSW, LSW
Chief Executive Officer, YWCA Bergen County
Helen Archontou
When it comes to health and fitness for women and girls, YWCA Bergen County has a history of being ahead of the curve. We offered physical education classes for girls from the moment our doors opened in 1920‚Äîdecades before the passage of Title IX. Our current facility was built in 1951 with fitness in mind, and the addition of an Olympic-sized pool in 1954 was coupled with the launch of our nationally-recognized American Red Cross Certified Aquatics Program. Today, it takes two pools to meet the community‚Äôs demand for swim instruction. We‚Äôve even added a successful satellite swim program in the City of Englewood, NJ.
Swimming may not be the first ‚Äúsport‚Äù you think of on National Women & Girls in Sports Day. But don‚Äôt tell that to the thousands of girls who‚Äôve taken swim lessons at our YWCA. For many of them, what began as something their parents insisted they learn literally became ‚Äúan investment in their futures,‚Äù igniting a passion for a sport they went on to play competitively. For others, it led to an unexpected and rewarding career.

Swim Instructor Lisa Prins
Lisa Prins is one of these girls. A YWCA lifeguard and swim instructor, she is one of three young women currently on staff who grew up in our pools. ‚ÄúI was four or five years old when I first started Little Dipper swim lessons,‚Äù she says. ‚ÄúI‚Äôm told that I was an overenthusiastic student who sometimes took my instructor under the water when I jumped in!‚Äù
Lisa took lessons at the YW until age 12, and returned several years later to train as a lifeguard. ‚ÄúThere was a summer camp where I wanted to be a counselor ‚Äî¬†but they really needed lifeguards, not camp counselors! I was always a strong swimmer and decided it was a great way to get a summer job.‚Äù Lisa returned to the YW in 2009, this time as a lifeguard and swim instructor.
YW Bergen mother/child swim lessons in 1955
Our swimming program is known for its one-on-one focus. Classes are small and the environment is welcoming¬†‚Äî perfect for instilling self-confidence along with a healthy respect for the water. Lisa encourages her students to do their best, challenging them to improve their strokes and increase their stamina the same way her teachers did. ‚ÄúLearning to swim is an incredibly important life skill ‚Äî¬†it can save your life or someone else‚Äôs.‚Äù She also is a lifeguard during the adult Aqua-Fitness program and has enjoyed seeing members‚Äô health and fitness improve over time. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs so important to feel empowered in the water‚Äîwhether you‚Äôre four years old or 74.‚Äù
Empowering girls to live active, healthy lives is something Lisa and our entire aquatics team does every day. Whether it‚Äôs gaining confidence during swim lessons; practicing teamwork as members of our Synchronized Swim team; or understanding goal setting while swim-team training in our Junior Swim Clinic, our YWCA strives to provide a safe and supportive space in which girls can learn, connect and own their power.
Helen Archontou has served as Chief Executive Officer of YWCA Bergen County since July 2011, and her focus is on guiding the organization towards living its name and its mission. This involves partnering with others in the community to broaden the YWCA‚Äôs scope of services, as well as developing mission-based initiatives aimed at empowering women and eliminating racism.
YWCA Bergen County is based in Ridgewood, NJ and serves the community at sites throughout the county. To learn more about all of our empowerment programs for women, girls and families, visit www.ywcaberngecounty.org.

The American Tarot Association is a professional and social organization for tarot readers, enthusiasts and scholars. They offer several programs that include educational courseware, publications, the Free Reading and Free Tarot networks (where people can get free readings from ATA members). The ATA also has regional, national and virtual conferences and outreach and service efforts. They encourage ethical conduct among tarot readers and ask that all members abide by their Code of Ethics (found at their website). The courses ATA offers are both for the public and for ATA members. This is a wonderful organization to join if you love tarot.
